        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 is a promising anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries due to high specific capacity, abundance, and low cost.  However, poor cycling stability, low rate capability and unclear electrochem. reaction mechanism are the main challenges for MoS2 anode in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, molybdenum disulfide/carbon (MoS2/C) nanospheres are fabricated and used for Na-ion battery anodes.  MoS2/C nanospheres deliver a reversible capacity of 520 mA-h/g at 0.1C and maintain capacity 400 mA-h/g for 300 cycles at a high c.d. of 1C, demonstrating the best cycling performance of MoS2 for Na-ion batteries to date.  The high capacity is attributed to the short ion and electron diffusion pathway, which enables fast charge transfer and low concn. polarization.  The stable cycling performance and high coulombic efficiency (∼100%) of MoS2/C nanospheres are ascribed to (a) highly reversible conversion reaction of MoS2 during sodiation/desodiation as evidenced by ex-situ x-ray diffraction and (b) the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interface layer in fluoroethylene carbonate based electrolyte as demonstrated by FTIR spectroscopy measurements.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1038/srep09254"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Membranes of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  This article reviews the recent progress in surface and interface engineering of electrode materials including the increase in contact interface by decreasing the particle size or introducing porous or hierarchical structures and surface modification or functionalization by metal nanoparticles, metal oxides, carbon materials, polymers, and other ionic and electronic conductive species.  Although significant progress has been recently made in the development of novel electrode materials, some crit. issues including low electronic cond., low ionic diffusion efficiency, and large structural variation have to be addressed before the practical application of these materials.         </div><div class="casAbstract">From the whole anode electrode of view, we report in this work a system-level strategy of fabrication of reduced graphene oxide (RGO)/SnO2 composite-based anode for lithium ion battery (LIB) to enhance the capacity and cyclic performance of SnO2-based electrode materials.  RGO/SnO2 composite was first coated by a nanothick polydopamine (PD) layer and the PD-coated RGO/SnO2 composite was then cross-linked with poly(acrylic acid) (PAA) that was used as a binder to accomplish a whole anode electrode.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are emerging as potential stationary energy storage devices due to the abundance and low cost of Na.  A simple and energy efficient strategy to develop electrodes for SIBs with a high charge/discharge rate is highly desirable.  By surface modification of Ge, using electroless deposition in SbCl3/ionic liqs., the stability and performance of the anode can be improved.  This is due to the formation of GexSb1-x at the surface leading to better diffusion of Na, and the formation of a stable twin org. and inorg. SEI which protects the electrode.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnO2 coated carbon cloth with surface modification as Na-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Fang, Xin; Ge, Mingyuan; Rong, Jiepeng; Shen, Chenfei; Zhang, Anyi; Enaya, Hani A.; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium (Na)-ion batteries offer an attractive option for low cost large scale energy storage due to the earth abundance of Na.  SnO2 is considered as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 1378 mA h/g.  However, several limitations, such as large vol. expansion with cycling, slow kinetics and low elec. conductance, have severely limited its performance.  In this article, we demonstrate an anode consisting of a SnO2 nanocrystal layer grown on hierarchical microfibers of carbon cloth (CC) with extra surface coating to addresses the above challenges assocd. with SnO2 anodes.  The soft nature of CC and the nanocrystal structure of SnO2 layers can effectively accommodate the vol. change assocd. with the sodiation process.  In addn., the effect from an extra coating layer of carbon (C/SnO2/CC) and Al2O3 (Al2O3/SnO2/CC) have been explored and the results showed that the extra coating layer can further enhance the performance of SnO2 anode.  The C/SnO2/CC core-shell structure anode achieved a 501 mA h/g and a 144 mA h/g capacity at 0.1 C and 30 C charge/discharge rate, resp.  Meanwhile, a 375 mA h/g specific capacity after 100 deep cycles with an 80% retention is achieved by Al2O3/SnO2/CC anode.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrode materials play a decisive role in almost all electrochemical energy storage devices, determining their overall performance.  Proper selection, design and fabrication of electrode materials have thus been regarded as one of the most critical steps in achieving high electrochemical energy storage performance.  As an advanced nanotechnology for thin films and surfaces with conformal interfacial features and well controllable deposition thickness, atomic layer deposition (ALD) has been successfully developed for deposition and surface modification of electrode materials, where there are considerable issues of interfacial and surface chemistry at atomic and nanometer scale.  In addition, ALD has shown great potential in construction of novel nanostructured active materials that otherwise can be hardly obtained by other processing techniques, such as those solution-based processing and chemical vapor deposition (CVD) techniques.  This review focuses on the recent development of ALD for the design and delivery of advanced electrode materials in electrochemical energy storage devices, where typical examples will be highlighted and analyzed, and the merits and challenges of ALD for applications in energy storage will also be discussed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1088/0957-4484/26/9/094001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic Layer Deposition of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> on Carbon Nanotubes/Carbon Cloth for High-Capacitance and Ultrastable Supercapacitor Electrode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanotechnology</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">26</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">094001</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Co3O4 nanolayers have been successfully deposited on a flexible carbon nanotubes/carbon cloth (CC) substrate by at. layer deposition.  Much improved capacitance and ultra-long cycling life are achieved when the CNTs@Co3O4/CC is tested as a supercapacitor electrode.  The improvement can be from the mech. robust CC/CNTs substrate, the uniform coated high capacitance materials of Co3O4 nanoparticles, and the unique hierarchical structure.  The flexible electrode of CNTs@Co3O4/CC with high areal capacitance and excellent cycling ability promises great potential for developing high-performance flexible supercapacitors.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms7929"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mai, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shan, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sup>+</sup> Intercalation Pseudocapacitance in Graphene-Coupled Titanium Oxide Enabling Ultra-Fast Sodium Storage and Long-Term Cycling</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in graphene-coupled titanium oxide enabling ultra-fast sodium storage and long-term cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chaoji; Wen, Yanwei; Hu, Xianluo; Ji, Xiulei; Yan, Mengyu; Mai, Liqiang; Hu, Pei; Shan, Bin; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6929</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are emerging as a highly promising technol. for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, it remains a significant challenge to develop an anode with superior long-term cycling stability and high-rate capability.  Here we demonstrate that the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in TiO2/graphene nanocomposites enables high-rate capability and long cycle life in a sodium-ion battery.  This hybrid electrode exhibits a specific capacity of above 90 mA h g-1 at 12,000 mA g-1 (∼36 C).  The capacity is highly reversible for more than 4,000 cycles, the longest demonstrated cyclability to date.  First-principle calcns. demonstrate that the intimate integration of graphene with TiO2 reduces the diffusion energy barrier, thus enhancing the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitive process.  The Na-ion intercalation pseudocapacitance enabled by tailor-deigned nanostructures represents a promising strategy for developing electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1088/0957-4484/26/27/274002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ren, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional SnO<sub>2</sub>@ TiO<sub>2</sub> Double-Shell Nanotubes on Carbon Cloth as a Flexible Anode for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanotechnology</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">26</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">274002</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-Like MoS2/Graphene Composites: Cationic Surfactant-Assisted Hydrothermal Synthesis and Electrochemical Reversible Storage of Lithium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Guochuang; Chen, Tao; Chen, Weixiang; Wang, Zhen; Chang, Kun; Ma, Lin; Huang, Feihe; Chen, Dongyun; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3693-3703</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A cationic surfactant-assisted hydrothermal route is developed for the facile synthesis of graphene-like MoS2/graphene (GL-MoS2/G) composites based on the hydrothermal redn. of Na2MoO4 and graphene oxide sheets with L-cysteine in the presence of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB), following by annealing in N2 atmosphere.  The GL-MoS2/G composites are characterized by X-ray diffraction, electron microscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and Raman spectroscopy.  The effects of CTAB concn. on the microstructures and electrochem. performances of the composites for reversible Li+ storage are investigated.  It is found that the layer no. of MoS2 sheets decreases with increasing CTAB concn.  The GL-MoS2 sheets in the composites are few-layer in the case of 0.01∼0.03 mol L-1 CTAB of hydrothermal soln. and single-layer in the case of 0.05 mol L-1 CTAB.  The GL-MoS2/G composites prepd. with 0.01-0.02 mol·L-1 of CTAB soln. exhibit a higher reversible capacity of 940-1020 mAh g-1, a greater cycle stability, and a higher rate capability than other samples.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of GL-MoS2/G composites for reversible Li+ storage could be attributed to an effective integration of GL-MoS2 sheets and graphene that maximizes the synergistic interaction between them.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2013.10.098"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mei, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of 3D Flower-Like MoS<sub>2</sub> Spheres with Nanosheets as Anode Materials for High-Performance Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Construction of 3D flower-like MoS2 spheres with nanosheets as anode materials for high-performance lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Ting; Chen, Yuejiao; Qu, Baihua; Mei, Lin; Lei, Danni; Zhang, Haonan; Li, Qiuhong; Wang, Taihong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors constructed 3-dimensional flower-like MoS2 spheres with nanosheets (&lt;10 nm) by a simple alc.-assisted solvothermal route.  The presence of alc. enhanced the dispersity of MoS2 samples, and the distd. H2O facilitated the formation of nanosheets through varying the vol. ratio of alc. and distd. H2O.  The prepd. MoS2 samples delivered high initial discharge capacity (1346 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1), good coulombic efficiency (77.49% retention for the 1st cycle and ∼100% for the subsequent cycles), excellent cycling performance (947 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 50 cycles) and remarkable rate behavior as anode materials for Li ion batteries.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D space-confined synthesis of few-layer MoS2 anchored on carbon nanosheet for lithium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Jingwen; Qin, Jian; Zhang, Xiang; Shi, Chunsheng; Liu, Enzuo; Li, Jiajun; Zhao, Naiqin; He, Chunnian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile and scalable 2D spatial confinement strategy is developed for in situ synthesizing highly cryst. MoS2 nanosheets with few layers (≤5 layers) anchored on 3D porous carbon nanosheet networks (3D FL-MoS2@PCNNs) as lithium-ion battery anode.  During the synthesis, 3D self-assembly of cubic NaCl particles is adopted to not only serve as a template to direct the growth of 3D porous carbon nanosheet networks, but also create a 2D-confined space to achieve the construction of few-layer MoS2 nanosheets robustly lain on the surface of carbon nanosheet walls.  In the resulting 3D architecture, the intimate contact between the surfaces of MoS2 and carbon nanosheets can effectively avoid the aggregation and restacking of MoS2 as well as remarkably enhance the structural integrity of the electrode, while the conductive matrix of 3D porous carbon nanosheet networks can ensure fast transport of both electrons and ions in the whole electrode.  As a result, this unique 3D architecture manifests an outstanding long-life cycling capability at high rates, namely, a specific capacity as large as 709 mAh g-1 is delivered at 2 A g-1 and maintains ∼95.2% even after 520 deep charge/discharge cycles.  Apart from promising lithium-ion battery anode, this 3D FL-MoS2@PCNN composite also has immense potential for applications in other areas such as supercapacitor, catalysis, and sensors.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/nn5020819"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tian, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, X.</span><span class="NLM_etal"></span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Scalable Growth of High-Quality Polycrystalline MoS<sub>2</sub> Monolayers on SiO<sub>2</sub> with Tunable Grain Sizes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">6024</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">6030</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a scalable growth of monolayer MoS2 films on SiO2 substrates by chem. vapor deposition.  As-grown polycryst.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cocatalysts have been extensively used to accelerate the rate of hydrogen evolution in semiconductor-based photocatalytic systems, but the influence of interface state between semiconductor and cocatalyst has been rarely investigated.  Here, we demonstrate a feasible strategy of two-dimensional (2D) nanojunctions to enhance solar hydrogen generation of the MoS2/TiO2 system.  Loading of 2D MoS2 nanosheets on the surface of 2D anatase TiO2 nanosheets with exposed (001) facets greatly increases the interfacial contact.  At an optimal ratio of 0.50 wt% MoS2, the 2D-2D MoS2/TiO2 photocatalyst shows the highest H2 evolution rate of 2145 μmol h-1 g-1, which is almost 36.4 times higher than that of pure TiO2 nanosheets.  The apparent quantum yield of hydrogen evolution system reaches 6.4% at 360 nm.  More importantly, the 2D-2D MoS2/TiO2 composite exhibits photocatalytic activity much higher than those of noble metal (such as Pt, Rh, Ru, Pd, and Au) loaded TiO2 photocatalysts.  The decisive factor in improving the photocatalytic H2 prodn. activity is an intimate and large contact interface between the light-harvesting semiconductor and cocatalyst.  The effective charge transfer from TiO2 to MoS2 is demonstrated by the significant enhancement of photocurrent responses in 2D-2D MoS2/TiO2 composite electrodes.  This work creates new opportunities for designing and constructing highly efficient photocatalysts by interface engineering.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/la049838g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ho, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, J.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation and Photocatalytic Behavior of MoS2 and WS2 Nanocluster Sensitized TiO2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ho, Wingkei; Yu, Jimmy C.; Lin, Jun; Yu, Jiaguo; Li, Puishan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Langmuir</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new approach has been developed for the fabrication of visible light photocatalysts.  Nanoclusters of MoS2 and WS2 are coupled to TiO2 by an in situ photoredn. deposition method taking advantage of the reducing power of the photogenerated electrons from TiO2 particles.  The photocatalytic degrdn. of Methylene blue and 4-chlorophenol in aq. suspension has been employed to evaluate the visible light photocatalytic activity of the powders.  The blue shift in the absorption onset confirms the size quantization of MS2 nanoclusters, which act as effective and stable sensitizers, making it possible to utilize visible light in photocatalysis.  Quantum size effects alter the energy levels of the conduction and valence band edges in the coupled semiconductor systems, which favors the interparticle electron transfer.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vertical single or few-layer MoS2 nanosheets rooting into TiO2 nanofibers for highly efficient photocatalytic hydrogen evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Chengbin; Wang, Longlu; Tang, Yanhong; Luo, Shenglian; Liu, Yutang; Zhang, Shuqu; Zeng, Yunxiong; Xu, Yuzi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Catalysis, B: Environmental</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The catalytic activity of molybdenum sulfide (MoS2) for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) strongly depends on the no. of exposed active edges of MoS2 nanosheets.  Making single or few-layer MoS2 nanosheets vertically stand on a substrate is a very effective way to maximally expose the edge sites of MoS2 nanosheets.  Vertically standing single or few-layer MoS2 nanosheets on porous TiO2 nanofibers (TiO2@MoS2) are successfully prepd. via a simple hydrothermal reaction.  Due to plenty of pores in the electrospun TiO2 nanofibers, the MoS2 nanosheets vertically grow from the inside to the outside, and the growth mode of the MoS2 nanosheets rooting into the TiO2 nanofibers endows not only intimate contact between TiO2 and MoS2 for fast electrons transfer but also high structural stability of TiO2@MoS2 heterostructure.  The vertical orientation of MoS2 nanosheets enables the active edge sites of MoS2 to be maximally exposed.  Without using Pt cocatalyst, the TiO2@MoS2 heterostructure achieves high photocatalytic hydrogen prodn. rates of 1.68 or 0.49 mmol h-1 g-1 under UV-vis or visible light illumination, resp.  This high photocatalytic activity arises from the pos. synergetic effect between the MoS2 and TiO2 components in this novel heterostructure.  In addn., the TiO2@MoS2 heterostructure exhibits a high durability as evidenced by the invariable hydrogen prodn. rate after continuous illumination over 30 h.  The work advances the development of highly efficient molybdenum sulfide-based HER catalysts.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/nn406156b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">David, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bhandavat, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Singh, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1759</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1770</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mechanistic Insight into the Stability of HfO2-Coated MoS2 Nanosheet Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ahmed, Bilal; Anjum, Dalaver H.; Hedhili, Mohamed N.; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4341-4350</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is demonstrated for the first time that surface passivation of 2D nanosheets of MoS2 by an ultrathin and uniform layer of HfO2 can significantly improve the cyclic performance of sodium ion batteries.  After 50 charge/discharge cycles, bare MoS2 and HfO2 coated MoS2 electrodes deliver the specific capacity of 435 and 636 mAh g-1, resp., at c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  These results imply that batteries using HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes retain 91% of the initial capacity; in contrast, bare MoS2 anodes retain only 63%.  Also, HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes show one of the highest reported capacity values for MoS2.  Cyclic voltammetry and XPS results suggest that HfO2 does not take part in electrochem. reaction.  The mechanism of capacity retention with HfO2 coating is explained by ex situ transmission electron microscope imaging and elec. impedance spectroscopy.  HfO2 acts as a passivation layer at the anode/electrolyte interface and prevents structural degrdn. during charge/discharge process.  Moreover, the amorphous nature of HfO2 allows facile diffusion of Na ions.  These results clearly show the potential of HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes, which performance is significantly higher than previous reports where bulk MoS2 or composites of MoS2 with carbonaceous materials are used.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref50" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/C2NR32758A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Comparison of Electrochemical Performances of Olivine NaFePO<sub>4</sub> in Sodium-Ion Batteries and Olivine LiFePO<sub>4</sub> in Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">780</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">787</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C2NR32758A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D780-787%26journal%3DNanoscale%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DC.%2BLuo%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26title%3DComparison%2Bof%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformances%2Bof%2BOlivine%2BNaFePO4%2Bin%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Band%2BOlivine%2BLiFePO4%2Bin%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC2NR32758A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13179&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC2NR32758A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Comparison of electrochemical performances of olivine NaFePO4 in sodium-ion batteries and olivine LiFePO4 in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Xu, Yunhua; Liu, Yihang; Luo, Chao; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">780-787</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-coated olivine NaFePO4 (C-NaFePO4) spherical particles with a uniform diam. of ∼80 nm are obtained by chem. delithiation and subsequent electrochem. sodiation of carbon-coated olivine LiFePO4 (C-LiFePO4), which is synthesized by a solvothermal method.  The C-NaFePO4 electrodes are identical (particle size, particle size distribution, surface coating, and active material loading, etc.) to C-LiFePO4 except that Li ions in C-LiFePO4 are replaced by Na ions, making them ideal for comparison of thermodn. and kinetics between C-NaFePO4 cathode in sodium-ion (Na-ion) batteries and C-LiFePO4 in lithium-ion (Li-ion) batteries.  In this paper, the equil. potentials, reaction resistances, and diffusion coeff. of Na in C-NaFePO4 are systematically investigated by using the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT), electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) and cyclic voltammetry (CV), and compared to those of the well-known LiFePO4 cathodes in Li-ion batteries.  Due to the lower diffusion coeff. of Na-ion and higher contact and charge transfer resistances in NaFePO4 cathodes, the rate performance of C-NaFePO4 in Na-ion batteries is much worse than that of C-LiFePO4 in Li-ion batteries.  However, the cycling stability of C-NaFePO4 is almost comparable to C-LiFePO4 by retaining 90% of its capacity even after 100 charge-discharge cycles at a charge-discharge rate of 0.1 C.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref51" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1021/nl4030352"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ko, Y. N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, S. B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, K. Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kang, Y. C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-Pot Facile Synthesis of Ant-Cave-Structured Metal Oxide-Carbon Microballs by Continuous Process for Use as Anode Materials in Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">13</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5462</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5466</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl4030352</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D5462-5466%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DY.%2BN.%2BKo%26author%3DS.%2BB.%2BPark%26author%3DK.%2BY.%2BJung%26author%3DY.%2BC.%2BKang%26title%3DOne-Pot%2BFacile%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BAnt-Cave-Structured%2BMetal%2BOxide-Carbon%2BMicroballs%2Bby%2BContinuous%2BProcess%2Bfor%2BUse%2Bas%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bin%2BLi-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnl4030352&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13179&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnl4030352&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">One-Pot Facile Synthesis of Ant-Cave-Structured Metal Oxide-Carbon Microballs by Continuous Process for Use as Anode Materials in Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ko, You Na; Park, Seung Bin; Jung, Kyeong Youl; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5462-5466</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper introduces a facile one-pot method for synthesizing a new structured material, named "ant-cave microball", by continuous ultrasonic spray pyrolysis.  The ant-cave-structured microballs are prepd. from a colloidal spray soln. with polystyrene nanobeads and sucrose.  Networking between the nanovoids formed by decompn. of the polystyrene nanobeads results in the formation of nanochannels.  The electrochem. properties of these ant-cave-structured MoO3-C microballs, prepd. as the first target material for lithium ion batteries, are investigated.  The nanochannels are uniformly distributed inside the microballs with MoO3 and carbon components uniformly distributed within the microballs.  Further, the microballs have initial discharge and charge capacities of 1212 and 841 mA h g-1, resp., at a c.d. of 2 A g-1, and the initial discharge and charge capacities based on the wt. of MoO3 (disregarding carbon component) are as high as 1814 and 1259 mA h g-1.  The microballs deliver a high discharge capacity of 733 mA h g-1 even after 300 cycles.  This is although microsized MoO3 powders with a filled structure have discharge capacities of 1256 and 345 mA h g-1 for the first and 300th cycles, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref52" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2003.10.016"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jow, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical Impedance Study on the Low Temperature of Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2004</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1057</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1061</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2003.10.016</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D49%26publication_year%3D2004%26pages%3D1057-1061%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DS.%2BZhang%26author%3DK.%2BXu%26author%3DT.%2BJow%26title%3DElectrochemical%2BImpedance%2BStudy%2Bon%2Bthe%2BLow%2BTemperature%2Bof%2BLi-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2003.10.016&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.6b13179&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2003.10.016&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical impedance study on the low temperature of Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, S. S.; Xu, K.; Jow, T. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2004</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1057-1061</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Science B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cycling performance of Li-ion batteries was studied by using electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  Results showed that total resistance of the Li-ion batteries is mainly composed of bulk resistance (Rb), solid-state interface resistance (Rsei) and charge-transfer resistance (Rct).  During cycling, the Rb and Rsei do not change while the Rct displays two min. in the same voltage regions where the major peaks of differential capacities are present.  The Rct can be linked to kinetics of the battery electrochem. reaction.  In response to the temp. change, the Rb and Rsei vary in a very similar manner, while the Rct shows significant difference.  In the fully charged and discharged states as well as at the low temps. (≤20°), the total resistance of the Li-ion batteries is predominated by the Rct.  Using the term of the Rct, we explained two low-temp. phenomena of the Li-ion battery: (a) charging of a fully discharged battery is much more difficult than discharging of a fully charged battery, and (b) both the power (operating voltage) and energy (delivered capacity) are substantially reduced.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript"         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201206854"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Goodenough, J.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Superior Low-cost Cathode for a Na-ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Long; Lu, Yuhao; Liu, Jue; Xu, Maowen; Cheng, Jinguang; Zhang, Dawei; Goodenough, John B.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium manganese hexacyanoferrate cathode materials with two structures can be synthesized at room temp.  The sodium-ion concn. in the aq. soln. during pptn. has a strong influence on the compn. and structure of the final product, resulting in different reversible capacity and cycling performance.  With higher Na+ concn., a cooperative Na+ displacement along a single [111] direction induces a transition from cubic to rhombohedral symmetry - this phase transition is reversible on cycling the Na+ concn.  Sodium manganese hexacyanoferrate with an initial rhombohedral structure exhibits a reversible capacity of 134 mA-h/g and retains 120 mA-h/g after 30 cycles.  The high power d. and high rate capability of this material make it a promising cathode material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c4cp00826j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahbi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tokiwa, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Negative Electrodes for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Research interest in Na-ion batteries has increased rapidly because of the environmental friendliness of sodium compared to lithium.  A review of recent scientific advances in the field of neg. electrode materials used for Na-ion batteries.  This paper sheds light on neg. electrode materials for Na-ion batteries: carbonaceous materials, oxides/phosphates (as sodium insertion materials), sodium alloy/compds. and so on.  These electrode materials have different reaction mechanisms for electrochem. sodiation/desodiation processes.  Moreover, not only sodiation-active materials but also binders, current collectors, electrolytes and electrode/electrolyte interphase and its stabilization are essential for long cycle life Na-ion batteries.  This paper also addresses the prospect of Na-ion batteries as low-cost and long-life batteries with relatively high-energy d. as their potential competitive edge over the commercialized Li-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Matsuda, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ishii, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cumings, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Expanded Graphite as Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2015.194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, H.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pasta, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorene-Graphene Hybrid Material as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat. Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials. It is an intriguing prospect, esp. for large-scale applications, owing to its low cost and abundance.  MoS2 sodiation/desodiation with Na ions is based on the conversion reaction, which is not only able to deliver higher capacity than the intercalation reaction, but can also be applied in capacitive storage owing to its typically sloping charge/discharge curves.         </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 is a promising anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries due to high specific capacity, abundance, and low cost.  However, poor cycling stability, low rate capability and unclear electrochem. reaction mechanism are the main challenges for MoS2 anode in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, molybdenum disulfide/carbon (MoS2/C) nanospheres are fabricated and used for Na-ion battery anodes.  MoS2/C nanospheres deliver a reversible capacity of 520 mA-h/g at 0.1C and maintain capacity 400 mA-h/g for 300 cycles at a high c.d. of 1C, demonstrating the best cycling performance of MoS2 for Na-ion batteries to date.  The high capacity is attributed to the short ion and electron diffusion pathway, which enables fast charge transfer and low concn. polarization.  The stable cycling performance and high coulombic efficiency (∼100%) of MoS2/C nanospheres are ascribed to (a) highly reversible conversion reaction of MoS2 during sodiation/desodiation as evidenced by ex-situ x-ray diffraction and (b) the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interface layer in fluoroethylene carbonate based electrolyte as demonstrated by FTIR spectroscopy measurements.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1038/srep09254"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Membranes of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci.         </div><div class="casAbstract">From the whole anode electrode of view, we report in this work a system-level strategy of fabrication of reduced graphene oxide (RGO)/SnO2 composite-based anode for lithium ion battery (LIB) to enhance the capacity and cyclic performance of SnO2-based electrode materials.  RGO/SnO2 composite was first coated by a nanothick polydopamine (PD) layer and the PD-coated RGO/SnO2 composite was then cross-linked with poly(acrylic acid) (PAA) that was used as a binder to accomplish a whole anode electrode. As a result, the designed anode exhibits an outstanding energy capacity up to 718 mAh/g at c.d. of 100 mA/g after 200 cycles and a good rate performance of 811, 700, 641, and 512 mAh/g at c.d. of 100, 250, 500, and 1000 mA/g, resp. Our results indicate the importance of designing interfaces in anode system on achieving improved performance of electrode of LIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1039/C6CP02364A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lahiri, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Olschewski, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gustus, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Borisenko, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Endres, F.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Surface Modification of Battery Electrodes Via Electroless Deposition with Improved Performance for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are emerging as potential stationary energy storage devices due to the abundance and low cost of Na.  A simple and energy efficient strategy to develop electrodes for SIBs with a high charge/discharge rate is highly desirable.  By surface modification of Ge, using electroless deposition in SbCl3/ionic liqs., the stability and performance of the anode can be improved.  This is due to the formation of GexSb1-x at the surface leading to better diffusion of Na, and the formation of a stable twin org. and inorg. SEI which protects the electrode.                         rightTab-cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnO2 coated carbon cloth with surface modification as Na-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Fang, Xin; Ge, Mingyuan; Rong, Jiepeng; Shen, Chenfei; Zhang, Anyi; Enaya, Hani A.; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium (Na)-ion batteries offer an attractive option for low cost large scale energy storage due to the earth abundance of Na.  SnO2 is considered as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 1378 mA h/g.  However, several limitations, such as large vol. expansion with cycling, slow kinetics and low elec. conductance, have severely limited its performance.  In this article, we demonstrate an anode consisting of a SnO2 nanocrystal layer grown on hierarchical microfibers of carbon cloth (CC) with extra surface coating to addresses the above challenges assocd. with SnO2 anodes.  The soft nature of CC and the nanocrystal structure of SnO2 layers can effectively accommodate the vol. change assocd. with the sodiation process.  In addn., the effect from an extra coating layer of carbon (C/SnO2/CC) and Al2O3 (Al2O3/SnO2/CC) have been explored and the results showed that the extra coating layer can further enhance the performance of SnO2 anode.  The C/SnO2/CC core-shell structure anode achieved a 501 mA h/g and a 144 mA h/g capacity at 0.1 C and 30 C charge/discharge rate, resp.  Meanwhile, a 375 mA h/g specific capacity after 100 deep cycles with an 80% retention is achieved by Al2O3/SnO2/CC anode.  The designed surface-coating/nanocrystal-active-material-layer/conductive-soft-platform core-shell system paves the way to high performance Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1039/C6RA02176J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">CdS/CdSe Co-Sensitized 3D SnO<sub>2</sub>/TiO<sub>2</sub> Sea Urchin-Like Nanotube Arrays as an Efficient Photoanode for Photoelectrochemical Hydrogen Generation</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">RSC Adv.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">37407</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">37411</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrode materials play a decisive role in almost all electrochemical energy storage devices, determining their overall performance.  Proper selection, design and fabrication of electrode materials have thus been regarded as one of the most critical steps in achieving high electrochemical energy storage performance.  As an advanced nanotechnology for thin films and surfaces with conformal interfacial features and well controllable deposition thickness, atomic layer deposition (ALD) has been successfully developed for deposition and surface modification of electrode materials, where there are considerable issues of interfacial and surface chemistry at atomic and nanometer scale.  In addition, ALD has shown great potential in construction of novel nanostructured active materials that otherwise can be hardly obtained by other processing techniques, such as those solution-based processing and chemical vapor deposition (CVD) techniques.  This review focuses on the recent development of ALD for the design and delivery of advanced electrode materials in electrochemical energy storage devices, where typical examples will be highlighted and analyzed, and the merits and challenges of ALD for applications in energy storage will also be discussed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1088/0957-4484/26/9/094001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic Layer Deposition of Co<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> on Carbon Nanotubes/Carbon Cloth for High-Capacitance and Ultrastable Supercapacitor Electrode</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanotechnology</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">26</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">094001</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Here we demonstrate that the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in TiO2/graphene nanocomposites enables high-rate capability and long cycle life in a sodium-ion battery.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A cationic surfactant-assisted hydrothermal route is developed for the facile synthesis of graphene-like MoS2/graphene (GL-MoS2/G) composites based on the hydrothermal redn. of Na2MoO4 and graphene oxide sheets with L-cysteine in the presence of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB), following by annealing in N2 atmosphere.  The GL-MoS2/G composites are characterized by X-ray diffraction, electron microscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and Raman spectroscopy.  The effects of CTAB concn. on the microstructures and electrochem. performances of the composites for reversible Li+ storage are investigated.  It is found that the layer no. of MoS2 sheets decreases with increasing CTAB concn.  The GL-MoS2 sheets in the composites are few-layer in the case of 0.01∼0.03 mol L-1 CTAB of hydrothermal soln. and single-layer in the case of 0.05 mol L-1 CTAB.  The GL-MoS2/G composites prepd. with 0.01-0.02 mol·L-1 of CTAB soln. exhibit a higher reversible capacity of 940-1020 mAh g-1, a greater cycle stability, and a higher rate capability than other samples.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of GL-MoS2/G composites for reversible Li+ storage could be attributed to an effective integration of GL-MoS2 sheets and graphene that maximizes the synergistic interaction between them.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2013.10.098"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mei, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lei, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of 3D Flower-Like MoS<sub>2</sub> Spheres with Nanosheets as Anode Materials for High-Performance Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile and scalable 2D spatial confinement strategy is developed for in situ synthesizing highly cryst. MoS2 nanosheets with few layers (≤5 layers) anchored on 3D porous carbon nanosheet networks (3D FL-MoS2@PCNNs) as lithium-ion battery anode.  During the synthesis, 3D self-assembly of cubic NaCl particles is adopted to not only serve as a template to direct the growth of 3D porous carbon nanosheet networks, but also create a 2D-confined space to achieve the construction of few-layer MoS2 nanosheets robustly lain on the surface of carbon nanosheet walls. As a result, this unique 3D architecture manifests an outstanding long-life cycling capability at high rates, namely, a specific capacity as large as 709 mAh g-1 is delivered at 2 A g-1 and maintains ∼95.2% even after 520 deep charge/discharge cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cocatalysts have been extensively used to accelerate the rate of hydrogen evolution in semiconductor-based photocatalytic systems, but the influence of interface state between semiconductor and cocatalyst has been rarely investigated.  Here, we demonstrate a feasible strategy of two-dimensional (2D) nanojunctions to enhance solar hydrogen generation of the MoS2/TiO2 system.  Loading of 2D MoS2 nanosheets on the surface of 2D anatase TiO2 nanosheets with exposed (001) facets greatly increases the interfacial contact.  At an optimal ratio of 0.50 wt% MoS2, the 2D-2D MoS2/TiO2 photocatalyst shows the highest H2 evolution rate of 2145 μmol h-1 g-1, which is almost 36.4 times higher than that of pure TiO2 nanosheets.  The apparent quantum yield of hydrogen evolution system reaches 6.4% at 360 nm.  More importantly, the 2D-2D MoS2/TiO2 composite exhibits photocatalytic activity much higher than those of noble metal (such as Pt, Rh, Ru, Pd, and Au) loaded TiO2 photocatalysts.  The decisive factor in improving the photocatalytic H2 prodn. activity is an intimate and large contact interface between the light-harvesting semiconductor and cocatalyst.  The effective charge transfer from TiO2 to MoS2 is demonstrated by the significant enhancement of photocurrent responses in 2D-2D MoS2/TiO2 composite electrodes.  This work creates new opportunities for designing and constructing highly efficient photocatalysts by interface engineering.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1021/la049838g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ho, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A new approach has been developed for the fabrication of visible light photocatalysts. The photocatalytic degrdn. of Methylene blue and 4-chlorophenol in aq. suspension has been employed to evaluate the visible light photocatalytic activity of the powders.  The blue shift in the absorption onset confirms the size quantization of MS2 nanoclusters, which act as effective and stable sensitizers, making it possible to utilize visible light in photocatalysis. In addn., the coupled systems are believed to act in a cooperative manner by increasing the degree of charge carrier sepn., which effectively reduces recombination.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.apcatb.2014.08.046"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zeng, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vertical Single or Few-Layer MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets Rooting into TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanofibers for Highly Efficient Photocatalytic Hydrogen Evolution</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Appl.                         rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vertical single or few-layer MoS2 nanosheets rooting into TiO2 nanofibers for highly efficient photocatalytic hydrogen evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Chengbin; Wang, Longlu; Tang, Yanhong; Luo, Shenglian; Liu, Yutang; Zhang, Shuqu; Zeng, Yunxiong; Xu, Yuzi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Catalysis, B: Environmental</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">164</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The catalytic activity of molybdenum sulfide (MoS2) for hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) strongly depends on the no. of exposed active edges of MoS2 nanosheets.  Making single or few-layer MoS2 nanosheets vertically stand on a substrate is a very effective way to maximally expose the edge sites of MoS2 nanosheets.  Vertically standing single or few-layer MoS2 nanosheets on porous TiO2 nanofibers (TiO2@MoS2) are successfully prepd. via a simple hydrothermal reaction.  Due to plenty of pores in the electrospun TiO2 nanofibers, the MoS2 nanosheets vertically grow from the inside to the outside, and the growth mode of the MoS2 nanosheets rooting into the TiO2 nanofibers endows not only intimate contact between TiO2 and MoS2 for fast electrons transfer but also high structural stability of TiO2@MoS2 heterostructure.  The vertical orientation of MoS2 nanosheets enables the active edge sites of MoS2 to be maximally exposed.  Without using Pt cocatalyst, the TiO2@MoS2 heterostructure achieves high photocatalytic hydrogen prodn. rates of 1.68 or 0.49 mmol h-1 g-1 under UV-vis or visible light illumination, resp.  This high photocatalytic activity arises from the pos. synergetic effect between the MoS2 and TiO2 components in this novel heterostructure.  In addn., the TiO2@MoS2 heterostructure exhibits a high durability as evidenced by the invariable hydrogen prodn. rate after continuous illumination over 30 h.  The work advances the development of highly efficient molybdenum sulfide-based HER catalysts.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1021/nn406156b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">David, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bhandavat, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Singh, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">8</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1759</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1770</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">New emerging large scale battery market has demanded low cost and high power or energy d. materials.  Sodium (Na) is a promising candidate for an anode material because of its low cost and natural abundance.  Also molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) is an attractive cathode material with layered structure.  In this study a Na/MoS2 cell was assembled to evaluate its electrochem. properties as a rechargeable battery.  In the first discharge Na/MoS2 cell showed two characteristic plateaus at 0.93 V and 0.8 V. Finally, Na/MoS2 reaction mechanism was suggested.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref48" class="rightTabRefNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit48" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA07064C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liao, J.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">De Luna, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Manthiram, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">TiO<sub>2</sub>-B Nanowire Arrays Coated with Layered MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is demonstrated for the first time that surface passivation of 2D nanosheets of MoS2 by an ultrathin and uniform layer of HfO2 can significantly improve the cyclic performance of sodium ion batteries.  After 50 charge/discharge cycles, bare MoS2 and HfO2 coated MoS2 electrodes deliver the specific capacity of 435 and 636 mAh g-1, resp., at c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  These results imply that batteries using HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes retain 91% of the initial capacity; in contrast, bare MoS2 anodes retain only 63%.  Also, HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes show one of the highest reported capacity values for MoS2.  Cyclic voltammetry and XPS results suggest that HfO2 does not take part in electrochem. reaction.  The mechanism of capacity retention with HfO2 coating is explained by ex situ transmission electron microscope imaging and elec. impedance spectroscopy.  HfO2 acts as a passivation layer at the anode/electrolyte interface and prevents structural degrdn. during charge/discharge process.  Moreover, the amorphous nature of HfO2 allows facile diffusion of Na ions.  These results clearly show the potential of HfO2 coated MoS2 anodes, which performance is significantly higher than previous reports where bulk MoS2 or composites of MoS2 with carbonaceous materials are used.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1039/C2NR32758A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Comparison of Electrochemical Performances of Olivine NaFePO<sub>4</sub> in Sodium-Ion Batteries and Olivine LiFePO<sub>4</sub> in Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">780</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">787</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-coated olivine NaFePO4 (C-NaFePO4) spherical particles with a uniform diam. of ∼80 nm are obtained by chem. delithiation and subsequent electrochem. sodiation of carbon-coated olivine LiFePO4 (C-LiFePO4), which is synthesized by a solvothermal method.  The C-NaFePO4 electrodes are identical (particle size, particle size distribution, surface coating, and active material loading, etc.) to C-LiFePO4 except that Li ions in C-LiFePO4 are replaced by Na ions, making them ideal for comparison of thermodn. and kinetics between C-NaFePO4 cathode in sodium-ion (Na-ion) batteries and C-LiFePO4 in lithium-ion (Li-ion) batteries.  In this paper, the equil. potentials, reaction resistances, and diffusion coeff. of Na in C-NaFePO4 are systematically investigated by using the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT), electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) and cyclic voltammetry (CV), and compared to those of the well-known LiFePO4 cathodes in Li-ion batteries.  Due to the lower diffusion coeff. of Na-ion and higher contact and charge transfer resistances in NaFePO4 cathodes, the rate performance of C-NaFePO4 in Na-ion batteries is much worse than that of C-LiFePO4 in Li-ion batteries.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper introduces a facile one-pot method for synthesizing a new structured material, named "ant-cave microball", by continuous ultrasonic spray pyrolysis.  The ant-cave-structured microballs are prepd. from a colloidal spray soln. with polystyrene nanobeads and sucrose.  Networking between the nanovoids formed by decompn. of the polystyrene nanobeads results in the formation of nanochannels.  The electrochem. properties of these ant-cave-structured MoO3-C microballs, prepd. as the first target material for lithium ion batteries, are investigated.  The nanochannels are uniformly distributed inside the microballs with MoO3 and carbon components uniformly distributed within the microballs.  Further, the microballs have initial discharge and charge capacities of 1212 and 841 mA h g-1, resp., at a c.d. of 2 A g-1, and the initial discharge and charge capacities based on the wt. of MoO3 (disregarding carbon component) are as high as 1814 and 1259 mA h g-1.
